  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText10233069227860136960" style="display:none">Time has passed since the apprentice and his master, Will and Halt, led the Araluens to victory against invaders, and Will is now a full-fledged Ranger with his own fief to look after. The fief seems sleepy -- boring, even -- until the Skandians show up and Will has to deal with the threat. Shortly thereafter, Will goes on a secret mission. Joined by his friend Alyss, Will is thrown headfirst into an extraordinary adventure propelled by fears of sorcery, and must determine who is trustworthy to the king and who is trying to take his throne.<br /><br />Will and Alyss must battle growing hysteria, traitors, and most of all, time. The king is fading, but when Alyss is taken hostage, Will is forced to make a desperate choice between loyalty to his mission and loyalty to his friend.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/187417-ummm-why-is-this-is-book-6-in-the">Ummm... Why is this is book 6 in the series? Is actualy book 5.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_187417'><a id="like_count_community_question_187417" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/187417?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F1524173.The_Sorcerer_of_the_North">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/187417-ummm-why-is-this-is-book-6-in-the">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2918779-asterop"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1601168663i/2918779._UY100_CR5,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2918779-asterop">Asteropê</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Someone numbered the wrong. They were going by chronological story-line, not the official publication order. I have edited and changed them to the off<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Someone numbered the wrong. They were going by chronological story-line, not the official publication order. I have edited and changed them to the official, publication listing, which puts them as such:<br /><br />5. The Sorcerer in the North (2006)<br />6. The Siege of Macindaw (2009)<br />7. Erak's Ransom (2006)<br /><br />Series can have listing that differ, to account for chronological story-lines, but as far as I know, the main, official series list should follow the official, publication order.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1338047847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1338047847" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1338047847?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781864719086" href="/book/show/15783742-the-sorcerer-in-the-north">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338047847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2271128404045564847"><i>Contains mild spoilers for this book and the prequels.</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_' title='The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sorcerer in the North</a> was, unfortunately, my least favourite of the series and probably the weakest sequel too. I was a little irritated by the beginning as it was set an entire <i>five years</i> after the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144350.The_Battle_for_Skandia__Ranger_s_Apprentice___4_' title='The Battle for Skandia (Ranger's Apprentice, #4) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Battle for Skandia</a>. but once I got used to an older will and the surrpisngly obvious lack of both Halt and Horace, it wasn't so bad... until we got pulled away from the new situation - again - and thrust into this new world of cl</span>
  <span id="freeText2271128404045564847" style="display:none"><i>Contains mild spoilers for this book and the prequels.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1524173.The_Sorcerer_in_the_North__Ranger_s_Apprentice___5_" title="The Sorcerer in the North (Ranger's Apprentice, #5) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sorcerer in the North</a> was, unfortunately, my least favourite of the series and probably the weakest sequel too. I was a little irritated by the beginning as it was set an entire <i>five years</i> after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144350.The_Battle_for_Skandia__Ranger_s_Apprentice___4_" title="The Battle for Skandia (Ranger's Apprentice, #4) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Battle for Skandia</a>. but once I got used to an older will and the surrpisngly obvious lack of both Halt and Horace, it wasn't so bad... until we got pulled away from the new situation - again - and thrust into this new world of cloak &amp; dagger (literally) espionage. I'm not saying I didn't enjoy this part - I did - but it was little too rushed. I just wished we had more time to adapt to the new circumstances. <br /><br />Anyway, the first two thirds kept me entertained as usual. I loved seeing this other side to Will, one where he got to be his usual open, friendly self and enjoy himself in public. The last third, however, was what I had a problem with. <br /><br />It was boring. There, I said. I didn't want to have to <i>ever</i> say that with this series but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/34049.John_Flanagan" title="John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">John Flanagan</a> managed to write four solid books so I'll give him that. I found the mysteries' conclusion unsatisfying and even a little anticlimactic. But I did like the fact that there was an escape attempt made that didn't work - it is nice to know that even the best Rangers cannot be perfect every time. <br /><br />I also just missed Halt, Horace, Evanlynn and even Erak. <br /><br />This series remains a favourite of mine, and I really did njoy this book. It just wasn't as good as the last four. Now, as always I'll end by saying that I am excited to go pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1814843.The_Siege_of_Macindaw__Ranger_s_Apprentice___6_" title="The Siege of Macindaw (Ranger's Apprentice, #6) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Siege of Macindaw</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2271128404045564847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8042416634096362071">Very good. One of the best in the series. Audio is superbly narrated by William Zappa, but I didn't care for the musical intrusions after each chapter. <br/><br/>However, the story is good. Moving at a fast pace, it feels like an adventurous alternative history set in a re-named England (Araluen), in the days of kings, knights, castles, and fiefdoms. No elves. No dragons. <br/><br/>Recurring key characters from prior series include Will the ranger and Alyss the courier diplomat (both are now adults, not apprentices</span>
  <span id="freeText8042416634096362071" style="display:none">Very good. One of the best in the series. Audio is superbly narrated by William Zappa, but I didn't care for the musical intrusions after each chapter. <br /><br />However, the story is good. Moving at a fast pace, it feels like an adventurous alternative history set in a re-named England (Araluen), in the days of kings, knights, castles, and fiefdoms. No elves. No dragons. <br /><br />Recurring key characters from prior series include Will the ranger and Alyss the courier diplomat (both are now adults, not apprentices, about 21 years old). We also see the master rangers again, Crawley and Halt.<br /><br /> Important new characters include an injured dog, a traveling minstrel dubbed Berigan, Baron Urgal of Seacliff (an island fief), and some Skandians (Vikings) led by Gunda Hardstriker. And let's not forget the nasty John Buttle, and all the frightened — and frightening — inhabitants of Norgate fiefdom, and an ugly fortress on the border of Picta (Scotland). Let's not forget the strange beings in Grimsdal Wood.<br /><br />Be warned — it ends on a cliff. This particular plot is completed in the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1814843.The_Siege_of_Macindaw__Ranger_s_Apprentice___6_" title="The Siege of Macindaw (Ranger's Apprentice, #6) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Siege of Macindaw</a>. <br /><br />Map here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.worldofjohnflanagan.com/rangers-apprentice/map/">http://www.worldofjohnflanagan.com/ra...</a></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269135984" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4442827-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310965151p2/4442827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269135984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12335639007951301330">This series just keeps getting better and better. I was a little nervous when there was a several years jump in-between this book and the last, and there were a few things that were glossed over in this jump (romance) that I wish I had gotten to explore with the characters, but I still enjoyed this book very much.<br/><br/>Will is finally a full Ranger, and is out on his own. While most of his growth happened in books 1-4, it is easy to see how much more he has improved in the skip of a few years, and his</span>
  <span id="freeText12335639007951301330" style="display:none">This series just keeps getting better and better. I was a little nervous when there was a several years jump in-between this book and the last, and there were a few things that were glossed over in this jump (romance) that I wish I had gotten to explore with the characters, but I still enjoyed this book very much.<br /><br />Will is finally a full Ranger, and is out on his own. While most of his growth happened in books 1-4, it is easy to see how much more he has improved in the skip of a few years, and his heightened skills are shown very well through his actions, and he is no longer expecting others such as Halt to come and save him. Will has to solve his own problems, and I really enjoyed seeing how much he had grown up.<br /><br />The humor, as always was great, and I loved that his childhood friend Alyss was finally given a bigger role, and how she was able to grow into more of an actual character, instead of just feeling like stock.<br /><br />The ending was as intense as ever, and left me wanting more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12335639007951301330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114540360" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114540360?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Braden Bell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Braden Bell" href="/user/show/3484765-braden-bell">Braden Bell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114540360" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4007222931333159811">I'm a fan of this series, but I felt that Flanagan started doing some great things in this book. It's Will's first adventure alone, and I was happy to see an increased role for Alyss. Flanagan has found a way, in my opinion, to credibly give his female characters important things to do in the context of a medieval world. <br/><br/>This book had some themes I think are especially important for adolescents to read--being popular vs. being good, the idea of appearances and making judgments on those appearanc</span>
  <span id="freeText4007222931333159811" style="display:none">I'm a fan of this series, but I felt that Flanagan started doing some great things in this book. It's Will's first adventure alone, and I was happy to see an increased role for Alyss. Flanagan has found a way, in my opinion, to credibly give his female characters important things to do in the context of a medieval world. <br /><br />This book had some themes I think are especially important for adolescents to read--being popular vs. being good, the idea of appearances and making judgments on those appearances, and the throes and challenges of young love. <br /><br />I really think these books are great for young men especially. They are heroic and action packed. They demonstrate concepts of traditional masculinity that are disappearing: strength, honor, bravery. But the heroes are as likely to carry the day through their wits and intelligence as brawn and skill. They are also respectful of women, and there are good female characters as well (although the books tend a little more towards the male point of view)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4007222931333159811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17294257441594091679"> Once you're really into this book, you can't stop reading. The only problem was that, for me at least, the first half didn't really grab my interest. It was quite boring, what with all the details and half of the book talking solely about Will's to-be mission.   <span id="freeText17294257441594091679" style="display:none"> Once you're really into this book, you can't stop reading. The only problem was that, for me at least, the first half didn't really grab my interest. It was quite boring, what with all the details and half of the book talking solely about Will's to-be mission. I wanted to get <i>to</i> the mission and once I did, I couldn't put the book down.<br><br>What I liked most about the novel was the element of mystery. In most of Flanagan's other books, the antagonist and protagonist are both clear as daylight, but in The Sorcerer of the North, the reader, along with the characters, tries to put the clues together to discover who's who, which was pretty fun. The conclusion to the mystery wasn't unexpected but it was pretty reasonable.<br><br><i>"I'm getting Alyss out of your damned castle- if I have to take it apart stone by stone to do it." </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380404777ra/787987.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>YES!! <span id="freeTextContainer7918351937515468661"><br/>Review from July 2016:<br/>WHAT? These books have had cliff hangers before, but this is the worst one yet!!<br/><br/>3.5 stars<br/><br/>I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8524612.Erak_s_Ransom__Ranger_s_Aprentice___7_' title='Erak's Ransom (Ranger's Aprentice, #7) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Erak's Ransom</a> before I read this one, and I'm glad I did.   <span id="freeText7918351937515468661" style="display:none"><br />Review from July 2016:<br />WHAT? These books have had cliff hangers before, but this is the worst one yet!!<br /><br />3.5 stars<br /><br />I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8524612.Erak_s_Ransom__Ranger_s_Aprentice___7_" title="Erak's Ransom (Ranger's Aprentice, #7) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Erak's Ransom</a> before I read this one, and I'm glad I did. Reading the stories chronologically gives them a better flow.<br /><br />This book was really good, but I liked some of the other stories better. The pacing of this book is on the slow side, and the mystery is not quite as interesting. I missed the supporting characters too. I'm hoping we will see more of them in the next book. One thing I found really unbelievable was that Will had the dog for two weeks, and it was perfectly trained in that time. I don't know any dog that is perfectly obedient in two weeks....<br /><br />I listened to the audio version of this, which was fabulous! My only problem was that Halt was given a Scottish lilt to his accent. I had not pictured Halt that way, so it kept throwing me off whenever Halt would speak. I never got used to it because Halt wasn't in this story much though, which is sad.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12230639547043635695">The Rangers Apprentice series by John Flanagan is truly one of the best series I've read so far in the world of reading. This is one of those books where you are just so compelled to keep on reading. I'm not a huge bookworm most of the time, but these books are incredible!<br/><br/>The series takes place in a vast land of kingdoms, battles, and sorcery. Will is centered in Sea Cliff fief temporarily until he is sent to the Northern lands as a jongluer. It is foretold that sorcery is about and a small cast</span>
  <span id="freeText12230639547043635695" style="display:none">The Rangers Apprentice series by John Flanagan is truly one of the best series I've read so far in the world of reading. This is one of those books where you are just so compelled to keep on reading. I'm not a huge bookworm most of the time, but these books are incredible!<br /><br />The series takes place in a vast land of kingdoms, battles, and sorcery. Will is centered in Sea Cliff fief temporarily until he is sent to the Northern lands as a jongluer. It is foretold that sorcery is about and a small castle is in need of help before being taken hold of the Scotti warriors. Its turns out Will is going to be a larger help then expected....<br /><br />This Rangers Apprentice book is incredibly detailed and descriptive, as all the other books are in the series, so much that it makes you feel as if you are right there with them on their adventure. As if it wasn't captivating enough almost every chapter is left with a cliff hanger that forces you to read the next chapter!<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anybody having an interest with medieval times, or if you are a fan of Alex Rider or something along those lines. This book won't disappoint you!</span>

  <span id="freeText15119247903679038013" style="display:none">In the past,I always considered this book to be a bit of a bore; I'm not sure why I ever thought that!<br />The story line is good, and it's exciting to read about Will on his first mission!         <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/714617-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2371083099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13463978297629563113">This children's book legit justifies, rationalizes, and *recommends* slavery via the main character, another primary character, and a secondary character, all of whom are cast as noble. SLAVERY. <br/><br/>I am not surprised but am deeply saddened and angered by how many reviewers fail to be bothered by this book's early, explicit, not-even-lowkey defense of chattel slavery. The author wrote these books for his son? And includes a defense of slavery in the fifth volume? What a legacy...</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2284616581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2284616581" />
    <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss"><img alt="C.P. Cabaniss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468698183p2/9656259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2284616581?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.P. Cabaniss" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss">C.P. Cabaniss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284616581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9051788039455407462">One of my reading goals this year was to read some of the series that I have ignored, despite the fact that I was enjoying them. This was one of those series. I read the first four a few years ago and really enjoyed them, then I just didn't pick up the next one. Which isn't really like me. <br/><br/>Anyway, this one jumps forward a few years in the story and Will has become a full Ranger. In some ways this was a good jump for me because it was so long since I read the last book. I didn't feel as lost as I</span>
  <span id="freeText9051788039455407462" style="display:none">One of my reading goals this year was to read some of the series that I have ignored, despite the fact that I was enjoying them. This was one of those series. I read the first four a few years ago and really enjoyed them, then I just didn't pick up the next one. Which isn't really like me. <br /><br />Anyway, this one jumps forward a few years in the story and Will has become a full Ranger. In some ways this was a good jump for me because it was so long since I read the last book. I didn't feel as lost as I might have if it had picked up directly after the previous story. <br /><br />Will was still likable and the story was interesting enough, but I didn't find myself very invested in this one. Maybe it's my current reading mood or the fact that I have been reading a lot more lately, but I found it a little more simple than I would have liked. <br /><br />I think this was still fun and it would make a good series for younger readers to get started on fantasy that isn't too deep and detailed. At this point though, I don't think I feel like continuing the series. With limited reading time, this isn't what I want to spend my time reading right now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9051788039455407462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152393213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152393213" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4764911-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294358717p2/4764911.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152393213?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/4764911-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4764911-natalie?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152393213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10220883499301043643">This takes place several years after the fourth book. Will is a new member f the Ranger’s Corps and has just become one of the fifty full-fledged Rangers of Araluen. Will has just received his first commission and the fief that he will be assigned to—Seacliff. It’s supposed to be really nice, quaint, quiet, nothing to crazy or dangerous. Afterall, he’s now the youngest Ranger in the Corps and this is his first fief. Life at Seacliff is much different from the life that Will Treaty is used to—he </span>
  <span id="freeText10220883499301043643" style="display:none">This takes place several years after the fourth book. Will is a new member f the Ranger’s Corps and has just become one of the fifty full-fledged Rangers of Araluen. Will has just received his first commission and the fief that he will be assigned to—Seacliff. It’s supposed to be really nice, quaint, quiet, nothing to crazy or dangerous. Afterall, he’s now the youngest Ranger in the Corps and this is his first fief. Life at Seacliff is much different from the life that Will Treaty is used to—he even has a last name from the Treaty that he helped to form between Skandia and Araluen with the new Oberjarl Erak who became a close friend of Will, Evanlyn, Horace, and Halt’s. Together they faced the Temujai army and were able to defeat and stop them from envading Skandia and spreading to Araluen. Thanks to Will and his friends the country has been at peace with Skandia for three years and the raids from the sea wolves have all but ceased. In Will’s life he’s learned that hard work is key and nothing is ever still for long in the life of a Ranger. Within the first month in his fief Will is given a challenge as the first raid from a Skandian crew comes to Seacliff and not only are the people unprepared but totally frightened of the prospect of losing their homesteads. Over the last few years their men have slacked, the people have slacked and they definitely aren’t trained or ready from an assault of any kind. Can Will handle the invading force on his own? Will he be able to spare the people of Seacliff from the raid, even though he’s young and feels virtually inexperienced? Will faces the Skandian crew, in Seacliff, the threat of sorcery, plots, ploys, and disguise as he undertakes the challenges of being a full-fledged Ranger and having to make the calls on his own.<br />This is another great book by John Flanagan about Will’s great adventures. He faces dangers and plots that all but overcome him as he battles to find the truth that seems to be evasive to the most skilled minds. Alyss joins the adventure as both take on a new identity in the hopes of being able to find a way to save their country from certain destruction. Well done and definitely attention-getting. This is a must read of John Flanagan’s and make sure that you have the sixth book close at hand as this one leaves you on a bit of a cliff-hanger!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10220883499301043643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_394192762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/394192762" />
    <a title="Evan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9205805-evan"><img alt="Evan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344791150p2/9205805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/394192762?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan" href="/user/show/9205805-evan">Evan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394192762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4148545356887509210">This book is really a great addition to the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br/> I am a fan of this series, as it includes a large amount of adventure, wit and great characters. For those who haven't read the series yet, I advise you do.<br/> This is the first book in the series where Will is finished his apprenticeship. When Lord Syron of the Norgate Fief in Hibernia is struck by a mysterious illness, Will, Tug, his new dog, and his friend/lover Alyss are called in to figure out what is ailing the Lord of No</span>
  <span id="freeText4148545356887509210" style="display:none">This book is really a great addition to the Ranger's Apprentice series.<br /> I am a fan of this series, as it includes a large amount of adventure, wit and great characters. For those who haven't read the series yet, I advise you do.<br /> This is the first book in the series where Will is finished his apprenticeship. When Lord Syron of the Norgate Fief in Hibernia is struck by a mysterious illness, Will, Tug, his new dog, and his friend/lover Alyss are called in to figure out what is ailing the Lord of Norgate.<br /> There are rumors of a dark sorcerer living in the Grimsdell Woods, called Malkallam, who has poisoned Syron. The villagers suspect the Black Art is involved. Will isn't so sure.<br /> Suspects are everywhere. Orman, the son of Syron, his cousin Keren the knight, Xander the assistant. Will must add the clues together, and figure out who poisoned Syron... before it's too late. The clock is ticking and Will might find allies in people he least expected.<br /> <br /> So overall, this book was pretty cool. It didn't have a large amount of action in it, only sporting one or two notable scenes that caused me excitement. I did, however, really like the new Will. He is a fully-fledged ranger now, and is capable of handling himself. He is a lot like Halt in some ways, but uniquely flawed and independent.<br /> My only problem with the book was the plot in general. It is basically like a darker-toned Scooby-Doo book. That's not saying I don't like Scooby-Doo. I'm just saying that I don't think he fits into the Rangers Apprentice. Still, John Flanagan entices me with his characters, who are very well built.<br /> There are a few minor plot twists, but nothing very shocking. Oh well...<br />OVERALL REVIEW<br /> 4.3 out of 5.0<br />CHARACTERS: Excellent. 4.6 out of 5.0 (if your thinking, "How do I come up with these figures?" I just make them up.<br />PLOT: Good. 3.8 out of 5.0<br />Starting Siege of Macindaw today. Thank goodness for Horace. Cool story needs more...GILAN!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_247386514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247386514" />
    <a title="Trisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4280826-trisha"><img alt="Trisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585779037p2/4280826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247386514?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha" href="/user/show/4280826-trisha">Trisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142414293" href="/book/show/6089263-the-sorcerer-of-the-north">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247386514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5220145002111213851">The Short and Sweet of It<br/>Will finally is set off on his own, but not to fight the straightforward, frontal assault enemies of the past. This time he is up against a legend, an elusive sorcerer rumored to be poisoning the king of a northern fief, a land integral to the protection of the whole kingdom.<br/><br/>A Bit of a Ramble<br/>As with all of the Ranger's Apprentice books, I loved the characters, the battle tactics, the weaving of plot lines, and the setting. Seeing Will strike out on his own was almost poi</span>
  <span id="freeText5220145002111213851" style="display:none">The Short and Sweet of It<br />Will finally is set off on his own, but not to fight the straightforward, frontal assault enemies of the past. This time he is up against a legend, an elusive sorcerer rumored to be poisoning the king of a northern fief, a land integral to the protection of the whole kingdom.<br /><br />A Bit of a Ramble<br />As with all of the Ranger's Apprentice books, I loved the characters, the battle tactics, the weaving of plot lines, and the setting. Seeing Will strike out on his own was almost poignant, like watching a nephew become an adult. I feel like I know Will, like I am somehow a part of his life, responsible for him or his therapist or something. I also enjoyed the pretext under which Will travels: that of a jongleur, a traveling musician, singing for his supper. This role is so different from Will the Ranger; as a jongleur, he is affable, outgoing, a bit goofy. It's nice to see this side of Will, pushed back because of his secretive, serious duties.<br /><br />I do have one problem with this installment however. The ending. Or rather, the lack thereof. While I appreciate the fact that a series is a continuance of the same story, I like my books to have a relatively full an complete plot. Books, even in a series, which just end with no resolution whatsoever, or in some cases even a climax, drive me bonkers. Everything is up in the air at the end of this one, an unexpected development in this so-far-self-contained series.<br /><br />This unsatisfactory ending is why this installment has received an Accept rating instead of a Borrow. While the story itself is just as entertaining as the rest, that one little travesty (in my opinion) really affected my overall judgment. I realize it's a quite specific pet peeve though, and not everyone feels the same as I do.<br /><br />In a strange irony, I've been flying through this series prior to this book. And now, when I really have to read the next installment to see what happens, I'm putting it off. I'm weird, what can I say?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5220145002111213851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86180224" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86180224?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781440720147" href="/book/show/6498260-the-sorcerer-of-the-north">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer86180224&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86180224" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14595894238523954045">I started this YA series back when I was running down audio books for my ill wife. It started out very well (I thought) and so i followed it. I mentioned before that I thought it "lost steam" in the captivity story and I wasn't that thrilled with it. This seemed to start out well with much of the "feel" Flanagain got in the earlier volumes. <br/><br/>I wasn't to thrilled with some of the book, it tells an interesting story and is somewhat absorbing. There were some "glitches" in that there are times that </span>
  <span id="freeText14595894238523954045" style="display:none">I started this YA series back when I was running down audio books for my ill wife. It started out very well (I thought) and so i followed it. I mentioned before that I thought it "lost steam" in the captivity story and I wasn't that thrilled with it. This seemed to start out well with much of the "feel" Flanagain got in the earlier volumes. <br /><br />I wasn't to thrilled with some of the book, it tells an interesting story and is somewhat absorbing. There were some "glitches" in that there are times that I think even pretty young readers wouldn't be taken in the way the Ranger (Will) seemed to be. Also, there was the scene when Will hanging a few stories above the ground at the barred window of "Alice's" (the romantic tension character) tower cell stops to have a conversation with her, as the wind whips around him and he tries to stand on a ledge we've already been told is icy. <br /><br />Still, I would probably have given this one a four star rating, but it stepped on one of my "pet peeve toes". This is a novel, given it's a YA novel, but it's a novel. It's not a comic book, it's not a "graphic novel", it supposed to be a novel. <br /><br />I hate novels that end in a blatant "cliff-hanger". It's like the writer wants to be sure you'll pick up the next "installment". Most books, even the ones with continuing underlying plots manage to tie up the "current" story lone a bit and not leave the heroine locked in a cell faced with possible death and the hero vowing to "save her if he has to pull the tower down a stone at a time".<br /><br />So, pretty good, but apparently only half a book. Three stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14595894238523954045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2007003484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007003484" />
    <a title="Johanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58260626-johanna"><img alt="Johanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473771266p2/58260626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007003484?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johanna" href="/user/show/58260626-johanna">Johanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58260626-johanna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007003484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1922166629650828538">The Sorcerer in the North is the fifth book in the Ranger’s Apprentice Series by John Flanagan.<br/>It starts several years after the last book ended. Will is now a full-fledged Ranger (can I say shame on you for not showing me that happening?) and has his first own fief to look after. But trouble quickly forces him to leave his new home and embark on a secret mission to figure out the truth behind mysterious occurrences in a castle on the northern border of Araluen.<br/>This books gives me what I loved a</span>
  <span id="freeText1922166629650828538" style="display:none">The Sorcerer in the North is the fifth book in the Ranger’s Apprentice Series by John Flanagan.<br />It starts several years after the last book ended. Will is now a full-fledged Ranger (can I say shame on you for not showing me that happening?) and has his first own fief to look after. But trouble quickly forces him to leave his new home and embark on a secret mission to figure out the truth behind mysterious occurrences in a castle on the northern border of Araluen.<br />This books gives me what I loved about the first books (badass characters with weaknesses and flaws) and adds a little more. <b> Will gets a doggie!!!! </b> Yes, I’m childish and I want a dog. Sue me. Also, he is finally of an age where romantic plot lines make sense so we can a tiny allusion to a romantic subplot … but it really is very tiny and shouldn’t bother anyone who doesn’t like romance in their books. Also, surprise, surprise, while these books so far were mostly just entertainment, excitement and fun, this one even had some social criticism!<br />My only complaint … it ends on a cliffhanger … again! Seriously, I feel like the author has a thing for having cliffhangers for most of his books. The second ended on a cliffhanger, the third kind of as well and now the fifth! Well, I’ll just have to go and find myself the sixth book now.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1922166629650828538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_33413204'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33413204-the-skeleth"><img alt="The Skeleth" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1569354140l/33413204._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('McS9uRCdbd1Ks1hQqWgVBh6Qb194x0eCcGbnXHboiJsL4tRrq8Okte2Y7DFenR/ZyM+Il7ZKyeUrGKHtu6t6AQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LSEq8ptImPw4Tq9o6Y2OFsI8HBSZ+O+jsvrRc2qNEk0XB0MgIBZRlJ9lGwkeeITJFGP73Fd1YcTphJfCp87g1w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer16373524556321703643"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/><br/>For mysteries by this same author, see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8307827.John_A__Flanagan' title='John A. Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>John A. Flanagan</a>.<br/><br/>John Flanagan grew up in Sydney, Australia, hoping to be a writer. It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It</span>
  <span id="freeText16373524556321703643" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />For mysteries by this same author, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8307827.John_A__Flanagan" title="John A. Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">John A. Flanagan</a>.<br /><br />John Flanagan grew up in Sydney, Australia, hoping to be a writer. It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>
